0439023521|1.0|Mark Twain defined a literary classic as \\"a book which people praise and don't read.\\"<br /><br />I've enjoyed reading classics since I was sixteen years old (a Poe anthology had me completely mesmerized!). I read George Orwell's 1984 during my early 20s, and it's by far one of the best books I've ever read.<br /><br />1984 can be considered a classic cyberpunk and dystopian novel.<br /><br />Cyberpunk can be defined as a genre that \\"is about expressing (often dark) ideas about human nature, technology and their respective combination in the near future.\\" (Cyberpunk Review)<br /><br />Dystopia (HUNGER GAMES = \\"YA Dystopia\\") can be defined as: \\"An imaginary place or state in which the condition of life is extremely bad, as from deprivation, oppression, or terror.\\" (The Free Dictionary)<br /><br />I was talking to a friend from the U.K. recently, who had this to say about commercialism:<br /><br />***<br /><br />\\"Wow! I never knew about BATTLE ROYALE. To be honest, I hated THE HUNGER GAMES without knowing anything about it. Partly it was because I kept seeing it in the Kindle best seller charts. I assumed it was just some badly written self-published garbage that had been hyped on Twitter. But I see now it has been hyped everywhere and has big money behind it.<br /><br />These big companies are businesses first and foremost. Stories are product. The ones they pick up are largely irrelevant. The marketing campaign is the main thing. Well, in fact the return on capital is the main thing. The marketing campaign is the way to achieve that. The product is just one small piece in the corporate plan.<br /><br />I have always been put off by commercialism in any media. In fact I'm prejudiced against commercially successful things. Too much trash is touted as worth our while. Journalists desperate for readers jump on any bandwagon they can. Things are famous because they are famous and not because of any intrinsic merit. This is truer now than it's ever been.\\"<br /><br />***<br /><br />I think it's scary how \\"dystopia\\" itself has become a marketing label. I think it's scary when people trash classic books as being \\"for pretentious people\\" only, while they praise modern-day bestsellers as being superior to classic books because \\"these books were more popular\\" than classic texts that (1) had some amount of depth to them, and (2) have stood the test of time. I think it's scary how quality doesn't seem to matter anymore, because some people see the 'elite' as being 'elitist'.<br /><br />Crass commercialism and corporate greed often go hand in hand. This is the real dystopia, where hype replaces meaning, where mediocrity is celebrated over something original and substantial, all in the name of profits. After all, how good can something really be if it can be replaced by another manufactured franchise in the next 5-10 years?<br /><br />Keep that in mind when the next hyped franchise comes around :)!<br /><br />-- author of THE HYPE GAMES: A HG Parody (Spring 2012; in \\"tribute\\" to everyone who stood up for BATTLE ROYALE and Stephen King's works)/><br />I think it's scary how \\"dystopia\\" itself has become a marketing label. 0545265355|5.0|I admit, I was a latecomer to the party with the Hunger Games.  I had the same knee-jerk reactions to the subject matter.  And in truth, I do find it a much more palatable rip-off of the much more adult and sicker Battle Royale manga series from the early 00s.  That said, it is a GREAT story.  When I first saw the movie, I had not yet read the books, so the movie takes on a slightly more sinister air.  But the complete story is very good, with echoing themes of 1984 and Animal Farm, with warnings to both government overreach and the capacity for power to corrupt.  Being this is a book for younger audiences, the book is a bit ham-handed and not extremely deep in its message, but that message is clear.  I really do like the insistence on the main characters that shades of gray are not acceptable, that there is good and evil, right and wrong, and evil deeds wrapped in good intentions are still evil.  These are very important lessons in any civil society.  Might does not necessarily make right.  With solid foundations such as these in their youth, hopefully some of that youthful idealism translates into future leaders making just and even-handed decisions.  In the end, isn't that what great art can do in society?<br /><br />The book is interesting in the fact it is told from the first person, from Katniss Everdeen, a young person's point of view, who has been thrust as a pawn into a much bigger game that she has little control over.  While her self-doubt and guilt tends to pile up and get a little tiresome, I think it is an accurate reflection on someone who feels powerless to control their own fate.  When Katnis steps up to change her fate, it is predictable, but still satisfying.  In the end, this is a fairly predictable, but rip-roaring yarn that is a pleasure to read.  It really sucks you in and does not let you go.  I finished all three books in about 2 weeks.  The pages just flew by.  I recommend it for readers 13 and up.

B004G6TCMQ|5.0|Nearly forty-two years after its recording, this eponymous debut album is still as expansive and interesting to me as when I first heard it in early 1971.  It's hard to believe that such masterful musicianship came from three guys in their early twenties, but gorgeous it was and continues to be.  Yes, \\"Lucky Man\\" was overplayed on the FM airwaves, but it's a great track, and I can still enjoy it.  My personal favorites are \\"Take A Pebble\\" and \\"Tank,\\" the latter possessing some of the finest power drumming this side of Buddy Rich.  The music on this album has a muscular freshness that grips you by the throat, lays you down gently, and then devours you at the end.  While later efforts may be seen as exercises in overblown commericalism, this first album delivered the band's initial effort with tasteful aplomb.  Emerson, formerly of The Nice, and Lake, fresh from King Crimson blended their talents with Carl Palmer (The Crazy World of Arthur Brown band) to craft something beautiul and uniquely their own.  Palmer's drumming is incredibly creative, and his technical virtuosity punctuates the band's sound with clean precision.  The crisp sound on this re-master is unprecedented in any former release.  This is an album that represents some of the finest rock classics of the decade, and is an absolute 5-star piece of work.

1416549447|4.0|Danny Dreyer's Chi Running: A Revolutionary Approach to Effortless, Injury-Free Running (New York: Fireside/Simon & Schuster, 2009) is now in its second edition.  It has been acclaimed by many coaches, runners and medical professionals, as reflected in its testimonials.<br /><br />Runners suffer many injuries. As Dreyer states, \\"It is estimated that 65% of all runners incur at least one injury a a year that interrupts their training.\\" (p. 2) Although over-training can cause injury, Dreyer's lays most of the blame on bad form.<br /><br />Dreyer credits his initiation to a T'ai Chi master, Zhu Xilin. The Chinese character for \\"chi\\" can be interpreted as \\"internal energy\\" and \\"t'ai\\" as \\"extreme.\\"  Many readers will be familiar with t'ai chi as a system of self-defense without weapons that includes a series of graceful exercises. I was apprehensive that Dreyer's reference to T'ai Chi might  be just a marketing gimmick, but the author in fact does forge a compelling connection between his principles and those of T'ai Chi (and, more broadly, other martial arts). T'ai Chi, like the Japanese martial art of jiu jitsu, seeks instruction from the grace and power of animal movements.<br /><br />Dreyer incorporates several elements from T'ai Chi practice into his style. The first is meditation/relaxation. The second relates to posture. The third is mindfulness of the body.<br /><br />Meditation and relaxation can help to relax the body. It's a truism that competitive athletics is largely a mental game, and for an endurance sport like the marathon, it's even more so. Instead of stretching before a race, Dreyer recommends movements to loosen keys joints and relax the muscles.<br /><br />Pose is an important element of T'ai Chi practice. For distance running, Dreyer recommends a slightly forward posture, \\"to allow gravity to assist your forward strides.\\" I am not sure as a matter of physics that this notion of gravity assist actually makes sense. I'd rather think of the leaning posture as a more optimal angle for our muscles to transfer energy to the ground. T'ai Chi, like other Chinese martial arts, focuses particularly on strengthening and pivoting off of the dian tien, which could be translated as the Core. In this respect, Western programs such as Pilates, the Alexander Technique and classic ballet instruction parallel a much older Eastern tradition. According to Dreyer, \\"80% of all the runners I teach start off by standing with their hips too far forward and their legs sloped to the rear, their shoulders back, and their knees locked\\"; Dreyer coaches these runners to create a \\"column\\" of correct posture for running.<br /><br />\\"Mindfulness\\" runs against the doctrine, \\"No pain/no gain.\\" If your body is experiencing pain, listen to it and make adjustments. Master Zhu taught Dreyer to let the chi run through the body as \\"water runs through a pipe.\\" Adjustments, he stresses, should be incremental, using your \\"Body Sense.\\" Correct breathing is a central aspect of mindfulness.<br /><br />Dreyer recommends using minimal running shoes of the sort sort by Vibram. Because these shoes lack padding under the heals, they encourage you to strike your foot more as you would as a barefoot runner. Dreyer recommends a full strike of the foot against the surface, rather than the typical heel to ball movement of most people using conventional running shoes. He gives a simple test of good form. Run on sand. If your tracks show the full tread markings of your shoe, you've struck correctly. If you're digging wedges into the ground with your heels (see photo on p. 90), you're using a poor technique that puts unacceptable strain on your legs, including especially your knees.  By the way, if your tracks are not parallel, that implies other problems that need correction. (I run in Vibrams but follow a ball-heel-ball striking pattern. I like the shock absorbing qualities of this striking pattern. But Dreyer is right that my way puts a lot of stress on the calves, and I'm going to try out his full strike technique. One more thing: Vibrams offer very little insulation against cold, so I would put them away if running on snow or ice. As an alternative to Vibrams, you might consider a light training show, less minimal than Vibrams, but with a weight of about 8-9 ounces; be sure the heel area is not pronounced, as that is the design Dreyer says encourages a bad striking pattern.)<br /><br />Dreyer finds that many injuries result from over-elongating the gait, while keeping too slow a \\"cadence.\\" Shorter steps with a faster cadence works better, he finds, to prevent injury. He recommends a steady cadence of about 80-85 strikes per minute. In effect, if you want to run slowly, decrease your stride, not your striking rate. There are some good examples of Dreyer's notion of \\"gearing\\" in his accompanying Chi Running DVD (sold separately).<br /><br />Dreyer  has helpful advice about rotation of the pelvis along what he calls the PivotPoint, which requires twisting of the spine. Also important is getting your arm swing right--the elbow at a right angle and arms swinging parallel, not across. He cites Duke Ellington's riff: \\"It don't mean a thing/if it ain't got that swing.\\" (p. 102)<br /><br />By the way, Dreyer has just published a new book, called Chi Marathon (Touchstone/Simon & Schuster, 2012). A posting by Deborah Kotz in the health blog of the Boston Globe discussed Dreyer's approach, which promises a \\"breakthrough natural running program for a pain-free half marathon and marathon.\\" . See Daily Dose, 3/26/2012. Whatever is true of running injuries in general goes double for marathons and ultra-marathons. Training injuries are almost the rule. He has also published a book and DVD on Chi Walking (New York: Fireside/Simon & Schuster, 2006).<br /><br />Mr. Dreyer manages three commercial websites related to these subjects: ChiWalking.com, ChiRunning.com and ChiLiving.com. The running Website usefully include training logs and programs.<br /><br />Dreyer Chi Running includes a series of photos of a female teacher or coach correcting a student's posture by \\"creating the column.\\" ( p.78) The photos reinforced my feeling that while reading a running book  and watching a DVD are good things, having a knowledgeable coach (perhaps someone trained by Dreyer) giving hands on feedback would be even better. In this light, I note that Dreyer offers programs to become \\"Certified Instructors\\" in Chi Running and in Chi Walking: He also offers help on his Website on finding a Certified Instructor.<br /><br />(The author of this review, Andrew Szabo, is founder of MindBodyForce.com)d I'm going to try out his full strike technique. B00756GKBA|5.0|There are several things I must address prior to delving into \\"MDNA\\". The first thing is that I was there with MTV in 1984 when \\"Borderline\\" and \\"Lucky Star\\" became smash hits that year. I was there, at age 11, when she performed \\"Like A Virgin\\" at the first VMA awards, bursting out of the wedding cake and writhing on the stage (me all uncomfortable as my parents looked on). And I was there for every Madonna moment thereafter. Yet, I didn't buy an album from her until 1989's \\"Like A Prayer\\" (which I will still argue with anyone that it is her best work). I was there through \\"Truth Or Dare\\", the sex book, \\"Erotica\\" (technically her low period). So what I am getting at before I review \\"MDNA\\" is that I have always liked Madonna, but I have also remained Madonna-neutral. That means I own all of her studio albums and respect her body of work, ahem. But I am not a blind zealot or an ignorant hater. I see her flaws, her immaturity, her narcissism, but I also see her overcoming the odds that were invariably stacked against her in the music business.<br /><br />That being said, I will boldly state that \\"MDNA\\" is one of her finer moments. Let me just remind the haters that Madonna started off as dance, and she has pretty much evolved her dance to current trends over the years, and she has done that quite well. \\"MDNA\\" is no different. So, vapid, asinine, ageist criticisms are irrelevant here. Plain and simple, Madonna cranks out one of her finest, most melodic, most invigorating dance albums in a long while.<br /><br />I bought the deluxe version with the extra disc of five bonus tracks. Listening to all 17 tracks back to back there are hardly any missteps here. \\"MDNA\\" has an edge over its sister companion, 2005's \\"Confessions On A Dancefloor\\" as \\"MDNA\\" has more attitude, tighter tracks, less late night dance club mixing. It surpasses 2008's \\"Hard Candy\\" with a more fluid, less stagnant approach. She stepped out of her comfort zone on \\"Hard Candy\\", which I respect, but ultimately came out with mixed results.<br /><br />First single \\"Give Me All Your Luvin'\\" and second single \\"Girl Gone Wild\\" are extremely infectious dance pop confections. \\"Girl Gone Wild\\" fully captures Madonna at her guilty Catholic girl best. \\"Give Me All Your Luvin'\\" embraces Madonna worship to its fullest. \\"Turn Up The Radio\\" is a radio friendly overcoming the mundane, at times depressing state of life. \\"Superstar\\" is Madonna sending her love out to her favorite person along with \\"Masterpiece\\". \\"I'm A Sinner\\" re-visits the guilty Catholic girl while \\"Love Spent\\" examines the exhaustion from being in a relationship. But it's her darker subject matter--\\"Gang Bang\\", \\"Some Girls\\", \\"Falling Free\\", \\"Beautiful Killer\\", \\"I F----- Up\\" and most directly and poignantly, \\"Best Friend\\" and \\"I Don't Give A\\" which all examine Madonna's feelings about past lovers (Guy Ritchie, perhaps, Sean Penn, Warren Beatty?) These tracks show a side of Madonna that is not often heard on record.<br /><br />Now, the haters can say all they want about how superficial and trite and contrived Madonna's 'self-expressions' are, and they may have some points, but you can't knock Madonna for putting down in words what sounds like the truth.
